1051<a target="object" rel="noopener" href="/pmc/articles/PMC5938896/table/T3/?report=objectonly">

1052Open in a separate window</a>

1053</div>

1054</div>

1055</div>

1056<div id="sec2-24" class="sec">

1057<h3 id="sec2-24title">

1058MS animal models utilizing delta-9-THC</h3>

1059<p id="__p38" class="p p-first-last">

1060MS animal models using autoimmune encephalomyelitis (EAE) have been used that demonstrate demyelination, neuroinflammation, and neurological dysfunction associated with infiltration of immune cells into the CNS consistent with the human disease. In certain types of mouse models of MS spasticity, &#x00394;9-THC has been shown to ameliorate spasticity and tremors.[<a href="#ref114" rid="ref114" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126292">

1061114</a>

1062] Activation of the ECS system in MS (and EAE) appears to limit neuronal damage by downregulation of cannabinoid receptors inhibiting GABA synapses as a protective action to reduce neuronal excitotoxic damage. Upregulation of endocannabinoid tone protects neurons from excitotoxicity in parallel with a therapeutic effect in a mouse model of MS.</p>

1063</div>

1064<div id="sec2-25" class="sec">

1065<h3 id="sec2-25title">

1066Human trials using &#x00394;9-THC for MS</h3>

1067<p id="__p39" class="p p-first">

1068Thus far, human trials with MS patients have been mixed using only 9-THC. In a 15-week trial with a tolerated dose of 9-THC, subjects had reduced urinary incontinence, and a 12-month follow-up demonstrated an antispasticity effect.[<a href="#ref3" rid="ref3" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126206">

10693</a>

1070,<a href="#ref36" rid="ref36" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126276">

107136</a>

1072] However, subsequent clinical trials did not demonstrate any effect on disease progression following long-term treatment with 9-THC.[<a href="#ref126" rid="ref126" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126181">

1073126</a>

1074,<a href="#ref127" rid="ref127" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126222">

1075127</a>

1076]</p>

1077<p id="__p40">

1078CBD acts specifically to enhance adenosine signaling which increases extracellular adenosine, not AG-2. Neuroprotective effects of CBD in hypoxic&#x02013;ischemic brain damage also involve adenosine A2 receptors. Specifically, CBD diminishes inflammation in acute models of injury and in a viral model of MS through adenosine A2 receptors.[<a href="#ref15" rid="ref15" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126271">

107915</a>

1080,<a href="#ref18" rid="ref18" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126284">

108118</a>

1082,<a href="#ref72" rid="ref72" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126202">

108372</a>

1084,<a href="#ref78" rid="ref78" class=" bibr popnode">

108578</a>

1086] CBD also ameliorates the severity of the disease by attenuating neuroinflammation and axonal damage through an effect on oligodendrocyte progenitor cells (OPC) that can be used to differentiate into new myelinating oligodendrocytes. OPCs are highly vulnerable to inflammation and oxidative stress. Inflammation contributes to demyelinating diseases such as MS. Synthetic cannabinoids studies have shown they can protect OPCs possibly by controlling endoplasmic reticulum (ER) stress response that modulates the response to inflammatory stimuli.[<a href="#ref79" rid="ref79" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126268">

108779</a>

1088]</p>

1089<p id="__p41">

1090Positive human clinical trials by GW Pharmaceuticals have permitted the pharmaceutical, Sativex&#x000ae; to be marketed for MS spasticity in 16 countries outside the U.S. It is an oral-mucosal spray containing a 1:1 ratio of plant extracted &#x00394;9-THC and CBD, having antispasmodic and analgesic properties shown to be effective for MS patients. The ability to modify pain may be attributed to a CB receptor-mediated regulation of supraspinal GABAergic and glutamatergic neurons. The results of these studies were cited in the AAN review.[<a href="#ref22" rid="ref22" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700445334">

109122</a>

1092]</p>

1093<p id="__p42" class="p p-last">

1094A meta-analysis in 2007 reported that CB receptor-based medications were superior to placebo in the treatment of MS-related neuropathic pain.[<a href="#ref58" rid="ref58" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126179">

109558</a>

1096,<a href="#ref78" rid="ref78" class=" bibr popnode">

109778</a>

1098,<a href="#ref93" rid="ref93" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126249">

109993</a>

1100,<a href="#ref94" rid="ref94" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126150">

110194</a>

1102,<a href="#ref121" rid="ref121" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126164">

1103121</a>

1104] This analysis evaluated 18 studies that included Sativex&#x000ae; (<em>

1105n</em>

1106 = 196), CBD (<em>

1107n</em>

1108 = 41), and dronabinol, Marinol&#x000ae;, &#x00394;9-THC only (<em>

1109n</em>

1110 = 91). Sativex&#x000ae; was reported to have the greatest effect to reduce neuropathic pain at 1.7 &#x000b1; 0.7 points (<em>

1111P</em>

1112 = 0.018), in a scale of 0 to 10. CBD 1.5 &#x000b1; 0.7 (<em>

1113P</em>

1114 = 0.044), dronabinol 1.5 &#x000b1; 0.6 (<em>

1115P</em>

1116 = 0.013) were slightly less and all cannabinoids pooled together 1.6 &#x000b1; 0.4 (<em>

1117P</em>

1118 &#x0003c; 0.001) and placebo 0.8 &#x000b1; 0.4 points (<em>

1119P</em>

1120 = 0.023). Dizziness was the most commonly observed adverse event with a slightly greater incidence in the Sativex&#x000ae; CBD/THC buccal spray. Overall, the analgesic response to cannabinoids was generally retained over time, at least for the 6&#x02013;10 weeks follow-up period.[<a href="#ref58" rid="ref58" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126242">

112158</a>

1122] Several preclinical studies have used CBD, for both spasticity and neurogenic pain, to augment existing pharmacological treatments. Further human clinical studies using CBD for MS are needed.</p>

1123</div>

1124<div id="sec2-26" class="sec">

1125<h3 id="sec2-26title">

1126Neuropsychiatric and brain trauma</h3>

1127<div id="sec3-4" class="sec sec-first-last">

1128<p>

1129</p>

1130<h4 id="sec3-4title" class="inline">

1131Cannabidiol </h4>

1132<p id="__p43" class="p p-first-last">

1133CBD is recognized as a nonpsychoactive phytocannabinoid. Both human observational and animal studies, however, have demonstrated a broad range of therapeutic effects for several neuropsychiatric disorders. CBD has positive effects on attenuating psychotic, anxiety, and depressive-like behaviors. The mechanisms appear to be related to the CBD's benefit to provide enhanced neuroprotection and inhibition of excessive neuroinflammatory responses in neurodegenerative diseases and conditions. Common features involving neuroprotective mechanisms influenced by CBD&#x02014;oxidative stress, immune mediators, and neurotrophic factors&#x02014;are also important in conditions such as posttraumatic stress disorder (PTSD), postconcussion syndrome, depression, and anxiety. Many studies confirm that the function of the ECS is markedly increased in response to pathogenic events like trauma. This fact, as well as numerous studies on experimental models of brain trauma, supports the role of cannabinoids and their interactions with CB1 and CB2 as part of the brain's compensatory and repair mechanisms following injury. Animal studies indicate that posthead injury administration of exogenous CBD reduces short-term brain damage by improving brain metabolic activity, reducing cerebral hemodynamic impairment, and decreasing brain edema and seizures. These benefits are believed to be due to CBD's ability to increase anandamide.[<a href="#ref109" rid="ref109" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126237">

1134109</a>

1135]</p>

1136</div>

1137</div>

1138<div id="sec2-27" class="sec">

1139<h3 id="sec2-27title">

1140Treatment with CBD</h3>

1141<p id="__p44" class="p p-first-last">

1142Treatment with CBD may also decrease the intensity and impact of symptoms commonly associated with PTSD, including chronic anxiety in stressful environments.[<a href="#ref11" rid="ref11" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126194">

114311</a>

1144] Exposure to stress can trigger anxiety in PTSD patients and remind them of traumatic experiences. In human studies, subjects introduced to fearful contexts exhibited decreased posttest anxiety when treated with CBD.[<a href="#ref5" rid="ref5" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126279">

11455</a>

1146] A human case report demonstrated that therapy with cannabis resin containing CBD helped to induce a significant reduction of symptoms of anxiety and depression in a teenage patient suffering from PTSD.[<a href="#ref96" rid="ref96" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700445337">

114796</a>

1148] By reducing induced anxiety, CBD may help to regulate the negative effects associated with PTSD. In rodent models, CBD effectively blocked the formation of fearful memories.[<a href="#ref112" rid="ref112" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126151">

1149112</a>

1150,<a href="#ref113" rid="ref113" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126186">

1151113</a>

1152] CBD may be an effective strategy to combat PTSD fear memory acquisition because of its direct effects diminishing the severity of traumatic memory. Rat trials also show CBD's potential in fear memory extinction, demonstrated through a significant decrease in freezing time when re-exposed to an anxiety-inducing situation.[<a href="#ref91" rid="ref91" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126154">

115391</a>

1154] Treatment with CBD has also been shown to attenuate contextual memories associated with past experience in murine experiments, showing CBD's ability to disrupt harmful memories.[<a href="#ref1" rid="ref1" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126267">

11551</a>

1156]</p>

1157</div>

1158<div id="sec2-28" class="sec">

1159<h3 id="sec2-28title">

1160Antidepressant and neuroprotective properties</h3>

1161<p id="__p45" class="p p-first-last">

1162Antidepressants, used for the treatment of depression and some anxiety disorders, also possess numerous neuroprotective properties, such as preventing the formation of amyloid plaques, elevation of BDNF levels, reduction of microglia activation, and decreased levels of proinflammatory mediators.[<a href="#ref82" rid="ref82" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126204">

116382</a>

1164] Similarly, CBD decreases the production of inflammatory cytokines, the activation of microglial cells, and brain leucocytes infiltration.[<a href="#ref79" rid="ref79" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126266">

116579</a>

1166]</p>

1167</div>

1168<div id="sec2-29" class="sec">

1169<h3 id="sec2-29title">

1170Rat models; efficacy of CBD in neurobehavioral disorders</h3>

1171<p id="__p46" class="p p-first-last">

1172In rat models of neurobehavioral disorders, CBD demonstrated attenuation of acute autonomic responses evoked by stress, inducing anxiolytic and antidepressive effects by activating 5HT1A receptors in a similar manner as the pharmaceutical buspirone that is approved for relieving anxiety and depression in humans.[<a href="#ref114" rid="ref114" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126250">

1173114</a>

1174] CBD experimentally attenuates the decrease in hippocampal neurogenesis and dendrite spines density induced by chronic stress and prevents microglia activation in a pharmacological model of schizophrenia. A double-blind, randomized clinical trial with CBD reported a significant clinical improvement similar to the antipsychotic amisulpride, but with less side effects.[<a href="#ref69" rid="ref69" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126158">

117569</a>

1176] Modulation of autophagy and enhanced neuronal survival have been reported using CBD in neurodegenerative experimental models, suggesting benefits of CBD for psychiatric/cognitive symptoms associated with neurodegeneration.[<a href="#ref10" rid="ref10" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126290">

117710</a>

1178]</p>

1179</div>

1180<div id="sec2-30" class="sec">

1181<h3 id="sec2-30title">

1182Human imaging studies correlated with CBD</h3>

1183<p id="__p47" class="p p-first-last">

1184Human imaging studies have demonstrated CBD affects brain areas involved in the neurobiology of psychiatric disorders. A study has showed that a single dose of CBD, administered orally in healthy volunteers, alters the resting activity in limbic and paralimbic brain areas while decreasing subjective anxiety associated with the scanning procedure.[<a href="#ref24" rid="ref24" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126218">

118524</a>

1186,<a href="#ref39" rid="ref39" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126153">

118739</a>

1188] CBD reduced the activity of the left amygdala&#x02013;hippocampal complex, hypothalamus, and posterior cingulated cortex while increasing the activity of the left parahippocampal gyrus compared with placebo. In healthy volunteers treated with CBD and submitted to a presentation of fearful faces, there was a decrease of the amygdala and anterior and posterior cingulate cortex activities and a disruption in the amygdala&#x02013;anterior cingulated cortex connectivity. In healthy humans, CBD reversed the anxiogenic effects of &#x00394;9-THC and reduced anxiety in a simulated public-speaking task.[<a href="#ref5" rid="ref5" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126289">

11895</a>

1190,<a href="#ref24" rid="ref24" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126246">

119124</a>

1192,<a href="#ref39" rid="ref39" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126172">

119339</a>

1194]</p>

1195</div>

1196<div id="sec2-31" class="sec">

1197<h3 id="sec2-31title">

1198Tetrahydrocannabinol</h3>

1199<p id="__p48" class="p p-first-last">

1200Interestingly, THC, administered prior to a traumatic insult in human case studies and animal models has had measurable neuroprotective effects. In a 3-year retrospective study of patients who had sustained a traumatic brain injury (TBI), decreased mortality was reported in individuals with a positive &#x00394;9-THC screen. In mouse models of CNS injury, prior administration of &#x00394;9-THC provided impairment protection.[<a href="#ref105" rid="ref105" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700445329">

1201105</a>

1202]</p>

1203</div>

1204<div id="sec2-32" class="sec">

1205<h3 id="sec2-32title">

1206Anxiety relief in humans</h3>

1207<p id="__p49" class="p p-first-last">

1208For anxiety relief in humans, variability in the responses to cannabis depends on multiple factors, such as the relative concentrations of &#x00394;9-THC and other phytocannabinoids. Studies have found &#x00394;9-THC facilitates fear extinction.[<a href="#ref2" rid="ref2" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126243">

12092</a>

1210,<a href="#ref45" rid="ref45" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126258">

121145</a>

1212] The 9-THC disrupts the reconsolidation of a fear memory in a manner dependent on activation of CB1.[<a href="#ref19" rid="ref19" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126197">

121319</a>

1214] In humans, oral dronabinol (synthetic 9-THC) prevents the recovery of fear. In general, conditions associated with chronic stress appear to be positively responsive to phytocannabinoids. Studies in rat models reported that cannabinoids prevented the effects of acute stress on learning and memory and improved neuroplasticity, behavioral, and neuroendocrine measures of anxiety and depression.[<a href="#ref1" rid="ref1" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126208">

12151</a>

1216,<a href="#ref8" rid="ref8" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126152">

12178</a>

1218,<a href="#ref17" rid="ref17" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126157">

121917</a>

1220,<a href="#ref91" rid="ref91" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126259">

122191</a>

1222,<a href="#ref96" rid="ref96" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700445326">

122396</a>

1224,<a href="#ref107" rid="ref107" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126223">

1225107</a>

1226,<a href="#ref112" rid="ref112" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126286">

1227112</a>

1228,<a href="#ref123" rid="ref123" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126193">

1229123</a>

1230,<a href="#ref128" rid="ref128" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126280">

1231128</a>

1232]</p>

1233</div>

1234<div id="sec2-33" class="sec">

1235<h3 id="sec2-33title">

1236Cancer</h3>

1237<div id="sec3-5" class="sec sec-first-last">

1238<p>

1239</p>

1240<h4 id="sec3-5title" class="inline">

1241CBD and THC </h4>

1242<p id="__p50" class="p p-first-last">

1243Cancer is a disease characterized by uncontrolled division of cells and their ability to spread. Novel anticancer agents are often tested for their ability to induce apoptosis and maintain steady-state cell population. In the early 1970s, phytocannabinoids were shown to inhibit tumor growth and prolong the life of mice with lung adenocarcinoma. Later studies have demonstrated cannabinoids inhibited tumor cell growth and induced apoptosis by modulating different cell signaling pathways in gliomas, lymphoma, prostate, breast, skin, and pancreatic cancer cells as well.[<a href="#ref26" rid="ref26" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126278">

124426</a>

1245,<a href="#ref76" rid="ref76" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126155">

124676</a>

1247]</p>

1248</div>

1249</div>

1250<div id="sec2-34" class="sec">

1251<h3 id="sec2-34title">

1252Utility for glioblastoma multiforme</h3>

1253<p id="__p51" class="p p-first-last">

1254Glioblastoma multiforme (GBM) is the most frequent class of malignant primary brain tumors. Both animal and human studies have demonstrated both &#x00394;9-THC and CBD, combined and separately, have significant antitumor actions on GBM cancer cell growth. The mechanism of &#x00394;9-THC antitumoral action is through ER stress-related signaling and upregulation of the transcriptional coactivators that promote autophagy.[<a href="#ref13" rid="ref13" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126247">

125513</a>

1256,<a href="#ref14" rid="ref14" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126239">

125714</a>

1258,<a href="#ref101" rid="ref101" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126221">

1259101</a>

1260,<a href="#ref102" rid="ref102" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126173">

1261102</a>

1262]</p>

1263</div>

1264<div id="sec2-35" class="sec">

1265<h3 id="sec2-35title">

1266CBD reduces growth different tumor xenografts</h3>

1267<p id="__p52" class="p p-first">

1268CBD has also been shown to reduce the growth of different types of tumor xenografts including gliomas. The mechanism of action of CBD is thought to be increased production of ROS in glioma cells, thereby inducing cytotoxicity or apoptosis and autophagy.[<a href="#ref71" rid="ref71" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126201">

126971</a>

1270,<a href="#ref74" rid="ref74" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126176">

127174</a>

1272,<a href="#ref75" rid="ref75" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126166">

127375</a>

1274,<a href="#ref76" rid="ref76" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126277">

127576</a>

1276] CBD is able to inhibit cancer cell invasion and metastasis mediated by inhibition of epidermal growth factor, NF-&#x003ba;B, and mTOR pathways. mTOR signaling pathway acts as the central regulator of cell metabolism, growth, proliferation, and survival, and is critical for tumor suppression. CBD also reduces angiogenesis through actions on both tumor and endothelial cells.[<a href="#ref111" rid="ref111" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126170">

1277111</a>

1278] The combined administration of THC and CBD is currently being therapeutically explored in human studies.[<a href="#ref26" rid="ref26" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126233">

127926</a>

1280,<a href="#ref71" rid="ref71" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126227">

128171</a>

1282,<a href="#ref110" rid="ref110" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126167">

1283110</a>

1284,<a href="#ref111" rid="ref111" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126187">

1285111</a>

1286]</p>

1287<p id="__p53" class="p p-last">

1288In Feb 2017, GW Pharmaceuticals announced positive results from a phase 2 placebo-controlled clinical study of their proprietary drug combining of &#x00394;9-THC and CBD in 21 patients with recurrent GBM. The results showed 83% one-year treatment group survival rate compared with 53% for patients in the placebo cohort (<em>

1289P</em>

1290 = 0.042). Median survival was greater than 550 days compared with 369 days in the placebo group. GW Pharmaceuticals has subsequently received Orphan Drug Designation from the U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA) and the European Medicines Agency (EMA) for their &#x00394;9-THC and CBD combination for the treatment of malignant glioma.[<a href="#ref47" rid="ref47" class=" bibr popnode">

129147</a>

1292]</p>

1293</div>

1294<div id="sec2-36" class="sec">

1295<h3 id="sec2-36title">

1296Intractable epilepsy</h3>

1297<div id="sec3-6" class="sec sec-first-last">

1298<p>

1299</p>

1300<h4 id="sec3-6title" class="inline">

1301Cannabidiol </h4>

1302<p id="__p54" class="p p-first">

1303Reports of cannabis use in the treatment of epilepsy appear as far back as 1800 BC. Scientific reports appear in 1881 from neurologists using Indian hemp to treat epilepsy with dramatic success.[<a href="#ref104" rid="ref104" class=" bibr popnode">

1304104</a>

1305] The use of cannabis therapy for the treatment of epilepsy diminished with the introduction of phenobarbital and phenytoin and the passage of laws prohibiting marijuana use in the U.S.</p>

1306<p id="__p55">

1307Experiments with &#x00394;9-THC have demonstrated a rebound hyperexcitability in the CNS in mice, with enhanced neuronal excitability and increased sensitivity to convulsions and has not been used on most trials of intractable epilepsy. CBD, however, produces antiepileptiform and anticonvulsant effects in both <em>

1308in vitro</em>

1309 and <em>

1310in vivo</em>

1311 models.[<a href="#ref64" rid="ref64" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700445336">

131264</a>

1313,<a href="#ref51" rid="ref51" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126183">

131451</a>

1315,<a href="#ref61" rid="ref61" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700445327">

131661</a>

1317,<a href="#ref62" rid="ref62" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126245">

131862</a>

1319,<a href="#ref63" rid="ref63" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126213">

132063</a>

1321,<a href="#ref85" rid="ref85" class=" bibr popnode">

132285</a>

1323]</p>

1324<p id="__p56">

1325More recently in 1980, Cunha <em>

1326et al</em>

1327., published a double-blind study that evaluated CBD for intractable epilepsy in 16 patients with grand-mal seizures. Each patient received 200&#x02013;300 mg daily of CBD or placebo along with antiepileptic drugs for up to 4 months.[<a href="#ref25" rid="ref25" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126264">

132825</a>

1329] They found in the treatment group 7 of 8 responded with fewer seizures. In the placebo group 1 of 8 responded with fewer seizures.[<a href="#ref25" rid="ref25" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126184">

133025</a>

1331,<a href="#ref124" rid="ref124" class=" bibr popnode">

1332124</a>

1333,<a href="#ref129" rid="ref129" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126203">

1334129</a>

1335] Since this report was published, there has been renewed interest in medical marijuana for clinical use, but most studies are isolated case reports and small clinical trials. These all suggest that CBD, the nonpsychoactive compound of cannabis, potentially can be helpful for controlling medication refractory seizures.</p>

1336<p id="__p57" class="p p-last">

1337As with most cannabinoid research to date, conducting studies can be difficult due to limited legal access to medical grade marijuana and phytocannabinoid extracts. Hemp-derived CBD, however, has recently experienced less regulation and as a result research using CBD for refractory epilepsy has experienced a resurgence.</p>

1338</div>

1339</div>

1340<div id="sec2-37" class="sec">

1341<h3 id="sec2-37title">

1342CBDs reduce neuronal hyperactivity in epilepsy</h3>

1343<p id="__p58" class="p p-first-last">

1344CBD's overall effect appears to result in reduction of neuronal hyperactivity in epilepsy.[<a href="#ref20" rid="ref20" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126295">

134520</a>

1346,<a href="#ref56" rid="ref56" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126216">

134756</a>

1348] As discussed earlier, the CB1 receptor is a presynaptic, G-protein-coupled receptor that activates voltage-gated calcium channels and enhances potassium-channel conduction in presynaptic terminals. While &#x00394;9-THC binds directly to CB1 receptors, CBD has indirect effects by increasing endogenous anandamide expression. Anandamide affects excitability in neuronal networks by activating the transient receptor potential (TRP) cation channel. CBD regulation of Ca2+ homeostasis via several mechanisms may contribute to these actions, particularly for partial or generalized seizures.[<a href="#ref62" rid="ref62" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126212">

134962</a>

1350]</p>

1351</div>

1352<div id="sec2-38" class="sec">

1353<h3 id="sec2-38title">

1354Endogenous cannabinoids</h3>

1355<p id="__p59" class="p p-first">

1356Endogenous cannabinoids appear to affect the initiation, propagation, and spread of seizures. Studies have identified defects in the ECS in some patients with refractory seizure disorders, specifically having low levels of anandamide and reduced numbers of CB1 receptors in CSF and tissue biopsy.[<a href="#ref97" rid="ref97" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126235">

135797</a>

1358] Additionally, the ECS is strongly activated by seizures, and the upregulation of CB1 receptor activity has antiseizure effects.[<a href="#ref27" rid="ref27" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126159">

135927</a>

1360]</p>

1361<p id="__p60">

1362The pharmaceutical company, GW Pharmaceuticals, is currently developing the CBD drug, Epidiolex&#x000ae; that is a purified, 99% oil-based CBD extract from the cannabis plant. Results of a recent 2015 open-label study (without a placebo control) in 137 people with treatment-resistant epilepsy indicated that 12 weeks of Epidiolex&#x000ae; reduced the median number of seizures by 54%.[<a href="#ref29" rid="ref29" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126174">

136329</a>

1364,<a href="#ref30" rid="ref30" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126269">

136530</a>

1366] Notably, subjects in this study ranged from 2 to 26 years old with an average age of 11. The dosing for CBD (Epidiolex&#x000ae;) was 2&#x02013;5 mg/kg per day, titrated until intolerance or up to a maximum dose of 25 mg/kg or 50 mg/kg per day (dependent on study site). Although this study exclusively looked for effects on seizure incidence, no evidence suggests that the antiseizure effects of CBD are limited to the treatment of this condition. Other open-label studies of Epidiolex&#x000ae; are ongoing in the U.S. Currently, The U.S. FDA has given permission to use this drug for &#x0201c;compassionate use&#x0201d; for a limited number of subjects with treatment-resistant epilepsy syndromes such as Lennox-Gastaut syndrome (a childhood-onset, treatment-resistant epilepsy characterized by multiple types of seizures and developmental delay) in children and adults and Dravet syndrome (a severe myoclonic epilepsy of infancy) in children. Development of synthetic forms of CBD is also in progress to treat seizure and other disorders responsive to the phytocannabinoid CBD.</p>

1367<p id="__p61" class="p p-last">

1368Despite the preclinical data by GW Pharmaceutical and anecdotal reports on the efficacy of cannabis in the treatment of epilepsy, a 2014 Cochrane review concluded that &#x0201c;no reliable conclusions can be drawn at present regarding the efficacy of cannabinoids as a treatment for epilepsy.&#x0201d; This report noted this conclusion was mostly due to the lack of adequate data from randomized, controlled trials of &#x00394;9-THC, CBD, or any other cannabinoid in combination.[<a href="#ref28" rid="ref28" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126256">

136928</a>

1370,<a href="#ref38" rid="ref38" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126214">

137138</a>

1372,<a href="#ref43" rid="ref43" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_848877177">

137343</a>

1374,<a href="#ref83" rid="ref83" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126169">

137583</a>

1376]</p>

1377</div>

1378<div id="sec2-39" class="sec">

1379<h3 id="sec2-39title">

1380Safety</h3>

1381<p id="__p62" class="p p-first-last">

1382A comprehensive safety and side effect review of CBD in 2016 on both animal and human studies described an excellent safety profile of CBD in humans at a wide variety of doses. The most commonly reported side effects were tiredness, diarrhea, and changes of appetite/weight.[<a href="#ref57" rid="ref57" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700445331">

138357</a>

1384] In studies comparing other medicinal drugs used for the treatment of these medical conditions, CBD also had a very favorable side effect profile. CBD does have interactions with common hepatic (drug)-metabolizing enzymes, belonging to the cytochrome P450 family. Therefore, interactions with drug transporters and interactions with drugs must be considered.[<a href="#ref6" rid="ref6" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126196">

13856</a>

1386]</p>

1387</div>

1388<div id="sec2-40" class="sec">

1389<h3 id="sec2-40title">

1390CBD &#x02013; better safety profile vs. other cannabinoids</h3>

1391<p id="__p63" class="p p-first">

1392CBD also has a better safety profile compared to other cannabinoids, such as THC. For instance, high doses of CBD (up to 1500 mg/day) are well tolerated in animals and humans. In contrast to THC, CBD does not alter heart rate, blood pressure, or body temperature, does not induce catalepsy, nor alter psychomotor or psychological functions.[<a href="#ref92" rid="ref92" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_819929905">

139392</a>

1394] This improved safety profile may be a result of its lack of direct agonist properties at cannabinoid receptors.[<a href="#ref4" rid="ref4" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126163">

13954</a>

1396]</p>

1397<div id="sec3-7" class="sec sec-last">

1398<p>

1399</p>

1400<h4 id="sec3-7title" class="inline">

1401Synthetic analog nabilone </h4>

1402<p id="__p64" class="p p-first-last">

1403A synthetic analog of &#x00394;9-THC, nabilone (Cesamet&#x02122;; Valeant Pharmaceuticals North America), was approved in 1981 for the suppression of the nausea and vomiting produced by chemotherapy. Synthetic &#x00394;9-THC, dronabinol (Marinol&#x000ae;; Solvay Pharmaceuticals), was subsequently licensed in 1985 as an antiemetic and in 1992 as appetite stimulant. The capability of &#x00394;9-THC for stimulating the CB1 receptor is paradoxically both the main reason for, and drawback against, its therapeutic use. In fact, as discussed below, psychotropic effects, and the potential risk of cardiac side effects, tolerance, and dependence, limit the application of &#x00394;9-THC as a synthetic or from a plant source in many therapeutic applications.[<a href="#ref87" rid="ref87" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126207">

140487</a>

1405]</p>

1406</div>

1407</div>

1408<div id="sec2-41" class="sec">

1409<h3 id="sec2-41title">

1410Adverse effects</h3>

1411<p id="__p65" class="p p-first">

1412The 2014 AAN review of 34 articles on MS using cannabinoids of various forms noted several adverse effects. Reported symptoms included nausea, increased weakness, behavioral or mood changes (or both), suicidal ideation or hallucinations, dizziness or vasovagal symptoms (or both), fatigue, and feelings of intoxication. Psychosis, dysphoria, and anxiety were associated with higher concentrations of THC. However, no direct fatalities or overdoses have been attributed to marijuana, even in recreational users of increasingly potent marijuana possibly due to lack of endocannabinoid receptors in the brainstem.[<a href="#ref66" rid="ref66" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126205">

141366</a>

1414]</p>

1415<p id="__p66" class="p p-last">

1416In a recent rule change by the World Anti-Doping Agency or WADA, CBD will no longer be listed as a banned substance for international sport competition for 2018. The agency noted that &#x00394;9-THC will still be prohibited. WADA issued with this ruling that noted CBD extracted from cannabis plants still may contain varying concentrations of THC.[<a href="#ref119" rid="ref119" class=" bibr popnode">

1417119</a>

1418] CBD extracted from the hemp plant has by definition &#x0003c;0.3% &#x00394;9-THC.</p>

1419</div>

1420<div id="sec2-42" class="sec">

1421<h3 id="sec2-42title">

1422Dosing</h3>

1423<p id="__p67" class="p p-first-last">

1424It is beyond the scope of this review to provide any meaningful dosing recommendations for CBD or &#x00394;9-THC. Like other cannabinoids, CBD produces bell-shaped dose&#x02013;response curves and can act by different mechanisms according to its concentration or the simultaneous presence of other cannabinoid-ligands.[<a href="#ref11" rid="ref11" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126234">

142511</a>

1426,<a href="#ref70" rid="ref70" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126229">

142770</a>

1428] In general, due to significant psychoactive properties of &#x00394;9-THC, the therapeutic dose range is limited by side effects. With a currently estimated 850 brands of marijuana-derived CBD products and 150 hemp-derived products on the market and an even greater number of various extracts of &#x00394;9-THC and marijuana plants cultivated to produce maximum &#x00394;9-THC concentration, universal dosing recommendations are nearly impossible.</p>

1429</div>

1430<div id="sec2-43" class="sec">

1431<h3 id="sec2-43title">

1432Prescribing medical marijuana</h3>

1433<p id="__p68" class="p p-first">

1434Ultimately, prescribing medical marijuana either as a primary treatment or adjunctive therapy will require extreme care and knowledge about the patient's goals and expectations for treatment. States that have allowed medical marijuana have generally required competency trainings and certification prior to prescribing. There are general screening questions that should be considered before recommending marijuana to a patient. At minimum, these questions should include the following:[<a href="#ref118" rid="ref118" class=" bibr popnode tag_hotlink tag_tooltip" id="__tag_700126285">

1435118</a>

1436]</p>

1437<p id="__p69" class="p p-last">

1438

1439</p>

1440<ul class="unordered" style="list-style-type:disc">

1441<!--

1442list-behavior=unordered

1443prefix-word=

1444mark-type=disc

1445max-label-size=0

1446-->

1447<li>

1448<p id="__p70">

1449Is there documentation that the patient has had failure of all other conventional medications to treat his or her ailment?</p>

1450</li>

1451<li>

1452<p id="__p71">

1453Have you counseled the patient (documented by the patient's signed informed consent) regarding the medical risks of the use of marijuana&#x02014;medical, psychological, and social (such as impairment of driving or work skills) and habituation?</p>

1454</li>

1455<li>

1456<p id="__p72">

1457Does your patient have a history of misused marijuana or other psychoactive, addictive prescription and illegal drugs?</p>

1458</li>

1459<li>

1460<p id="__p73">

1461Will you want periodic drug testing?</p>

1462</li>

1463<li>

1464<p id="__p74">

1465Will you know the standardization and potency content of the medical marijuana to be used and whether it is free of contaminants?</p>

1466</li>

1467</ul>

1468<p>

1469

1470</p>

1471</div>

1472<div id="sec2-44" class="sec sec-last">

1473<h3 id="sec2-44title">

1474FDA approvals</h3>

1475<p id="__p75" class="p p-first-last">

1476The FDA has approved the synthetic drugs Cesamet&#x000ae;, Marinol&#x000ae;, and Syndros&#x000ae; for therapeutic uses in the U.S. FDA-posted indications include nausea and the treatment of anorexia associated with weight loss in AIDS patients. Marinol&#x000ae; and Syndros&#x000ae; include the active ingredient dronabinol, a synthetic delta-9-THC. Cesamet&#x000ae; contains the active ingredient nabilone that has a chemical structure similar to THC and is also synthetically derived. Although these medications are often cited in human clinical research, their general use is limited based both on side effects and indication constraints.</p>

1477</div>

1478</div>

1479<div id="sec1-2" class="tsec sec">

1480<h2 class="head no_bottom_margin" id="sec1-2title">

1481CONCLUSION</h2>

1482<p id="__p76" class="p p-first">

1483Although federal and state laws are inconsistent about the legality of cannabis production, its increasingly documented health benefits make it once again relevant in medicine. Current research indicates the phytocannabinoids have a powerful therapeutic potential in a variety of ailments primarily through their interaction with the ECS. CBD is of particular interest due to its wide-ranging capabilities and lack of side effects in a variety of neurological conditions and diseases.</p>

1484<div id="sec2-45" class="sec">

1485<div id="sec3-8" class="sec sec-first-last">

1486<p>

1487</p>

1488<h4 id="sec3-8title" class="inline">

1489Legalization of marijuana in many states: Need for education </h4>

1490<p id="__p77" class="p p-first-last">

1491Because of the rapid legalization of medical marijuana by the majority of state legislatures in the U.S., physicians are faced with a lack of formal education and basic knowledge as to the possible indications, side effects, interactions, and dosing when prescribing medical marijuana. Because of federal restrictions on human research in the U.S., we lack the number and quality of human trials typically used when prescribing a medication. This review of the neurological benefits of phytocannabinoids has demonstrated significant benefits for neuroprotection and disease reductions in a wide variety of neurological diseases and conditions in humans.</p>

1492</div>

1493</div>
